pattern 1/60: PROVED cells=12 depth=2 diamonds=2 odd_wheels=1 circular_ladders=0 bridged_hexagons=0 set_equivalences=0 parity_transports=0 pigeonhole_xwings=0 guardians=0 branches=0 complete=true greedy_branches=0 greedy_odd_wheels=0 greedy_circular_ladders=0 greedy_bridged_hexagons=0 greedy_set_equivalences=0 greedy_parity_transports=0 greedy_pigeonhole_xwings=0 greedy_guardians=0 proofs=4
000000000000000000000000000000000000000000001001001010000001001001001100001010001
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r6c6, r7c6, r8c6, r9c5} (spine r7c6—r8c6).
      → color(r6c6) = color(r9c5). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c3, [r6c6=r9c5], r9c3, r9c9} (spine [r6c6=r9c5]—r9c3).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r9c9). Identify.
  3.  Odd wheel: hub [r6c3=r9c9] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {r5c9, r6c8, [r6c6=r9c5], r9c3, r8c3, r8c7, r7c9} (length 7) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 1/3 [no_diamond] (ladder+xwing+guardian) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Circular ladder {r8c3—r9c3, r8c6—r9c5, r8c7—r9c9}:
      Satellites r6c3 (rung 1), r7c6 (rung 2), r7c9 (rung 3) forced to distinct colors. Add triangle.
  2.  Guardian: r8c7 guards oddagon {r8c7, r7c9, r6c3, r6c6, r8c6} (source r7c6).
      → color(r8c7) = color(r7c6). Identify.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r6c3, [r7c6=r8c7], r9c5, r9c3}:
      Diagonals: {r6c3, r9c5} and {[r7c6=r8c7], r9c3} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r6c3) = color(r9c5) = X
        row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c8}: r6c3=X → r6c6, r6c8≠X
        row 9 {r9c3, r9c5, r9c9}: r9c5=X → r9c3, r9c9≠X
        col 3 {r6c3, r8c3, r9c3}: r6c3=X → r8c3≠X
        box 8 {[r7c6=r8c7], r8c6, r9c5}: r9c5=X → [r7c6=r8c7], r8c6≠X
        box 9 {[r7c6=r8c7], r7c9, r9c9}: [r7c6=r8c7], r9c9≠X → r7c9=X
        r6c3=X and r7c9=X are adjacent
        Contradiction.
      Case 2: color([r7c6=r8c7]) = color(r9c3) = X
        row 8 {[r7c6=r8c7], r8c3, r8c6}: [r7c6=r8c7]=X → r8c3, r8c6≠X
        row 9 {r9c3, r9c5, r9c9}: r9c3=X → r9c5, r9c9≠X
        col 3 {r6c3, r8c3, r9c3}: r9c3=X → r6c3≠X
        col 6 {r6c6, [r7c6=r8c7], r8c6}: [r7c6=r8c7]=X → r6c6≠X
        box 9 {[r7c6=r8c7], r7c9, r9c9}: [r7c6=r8c7]=X → r7c9≠X
        row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c8}: r6c3, r6c6≠X → r6c8=X
        col 9 {r5c9, r7c9, r9c9}: r7c9, r9c9≠X → r5c9=X
        r5c9=X and r6c8=X are adjacent
        Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 2/3 [no_oddwheel] (diamond+set) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r5c9, r7c9, r9c9, r8c7} (spine r7c9—r9c9).
      → color(r5c9) = color(r8c7). Identify.
  2.  SET: {row 6, row 8, row 9} − {col 3, col 6, col 9}.
      Remainder: {[r5c9=r8c7], r6c8, r9c5} = {[r5c9=r8c7], r7c6, r7c9}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  3.  K₄ on {[r5c9=r8c7], r7c6, r8c6, r9c5}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 3/3 [greedy] (diamond) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r6c6, r7c6, r8c6, r9c5} (spine r7c6—r8c6).
      → color(r6c6) = color(r9c5). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c8, r6c3, [r6c6=r9c5], r9c3} (spine r6c3—[r6c6=r9c5]).
      → color(r6c8) = color(r9c3). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {[r6c8=r9c3], r5c9, r9c9, r7c9} (spine r5c9—r9c9).
      → color([r6c8=r9c3]) = color(r7c9). Identify.
  4.  Diamond {[r6c6=r9c5], r6c3, [r6c8=r7c9=r9c3], r8c3} (spine r6c3—[r6c8=r7c9=r9c3]).
      → color([r6c6=r9c5]) = color(r8c3). Identify.
  5.  K₄ on {[r6c6=r8c3=r9c5], [r6c8=r7c9=r9c3], r8c7, r9c9}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r6c3, r6c6, r9c6, r9c9, r8c9, r8c3}
      Bridges: r6c8—r5c9 (edges r6c3—r6c6 ↔ r9c9—r8c9), r7c6—r8c5 (edges r6c6—r9c6 ↔ r8c9—r8c3), r9c2—r7c3 (edges r9c6—r9c9 ↔ r8c3—r6c3).

=== Alt proof 1/1 [no_hexagon] (xwing) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r8c3, r8c5, r9c6, r9c2}:
      Diagonals: {r8c3, r9c6} and {r8c5, r9c2} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r8c3) = color(r9c6) = X
        row 8 {r8c3, r8c5, r8c9}: r8c3=X → r8c5, r8c9≠X
        row 9 {r9c2, r9c6, r9c9}: r9c6=X → r9c2, r9c9≠X
        col 3 {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3}: r8c3=X → r6c3, r7c3≠X
        col 6 {r6c6, r7c6, r9c6}: r9c6=X → r6c6, r7c6≠X
        col 9 {r5c9, r8c9, r9c9}: r8c9, r9c9≠X → r5c9=X
        row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c8}: r6c3, r6c6≠X → r6c8=X
        r5c9=X and r6c8=X are adjacent
        Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r8c5) = color(r9c2) = X
        row 8 {r8c3, r8c5, r8c9}: r8c5=X → r8c3, r8c9≠X
        row 9 {r9c2, r9c6, r9c9}: r9c2=X → r9c6, r9c9≠X
        col 9 {r5c9, r8c9, r9c9}: r8c9, r9c9≠X → r5c9=X
        box 7 {r7c3, r8c3, r9c2}: r9c2=X → r7c3≠X
        box 8 {r7c6, r8c5, r9c6}: r8c5=X → r7c6≠X
        col 3 {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3}: r7c3, r8c3≠X → r6c3=X
        col 6 {r6c6, r7c6, r9c6}: r7c6, r9c6≠X → r6c6=X
        r6c3=X and r6c6=X are adjacent
        Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 2/2 [no_diamond] (set+branch+guardian) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r5c6, r9c5:
      Case A: color(r5c6) = color(r9c5). Identify.
        2.  SET: {col 6, col 8} − {box 8, box 9}.
            Remainder: {[r5c6=r9c5], r6c8} = {[r5c6=r9c5], r9c7}.
            → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
        3.  Guardian: r9c3 guards oddagon {r9c3, [r5c6=r9c5], r5c9, r6c9, r6c3} (source r6c8).
            → color(r9c3) = color(r6c8). Identify.
        4.  K₄ on {[r6c8=r9c3], r7c8, r8c8, r9c7}. Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r5c6) ≠ color(r9c5). Add edge.
        5.  K₄ on {r5c6, r7c6, r8c6, r9c5}. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 2/2 [no_ladder] (diamond+xwing+branch) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r8c2, r9c8:
      Case A: color(r8c2) = color(r9c8). Identify.
        2.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r6c3, r6c8, [r8c2=r9c8], r7c3}:
            Diagonals: {r6c3, [r8c2=r9c8]} and {r6c8, r7c3} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r6c3) = color([r8c2=r9c8]) = X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c8, r6c9}: r6c3=X → r6c8, r6c9≠X
              row 8 {[r8c2=r9c8], r8c6, r8c8}: [r8c2=r9c8]=X → r8c6, r8c8≠X
              row 9 {[r8c2=r9c8], r9c2, r9c6}: [r8c2=r9c8]=X → r9c2, r9c6≠X
              col 6 {r5c6, r8c6, r9c6}: r8c6, r9c6≠X → r5c6=X
              box 6 {r5c9, r6c8, r6c9}: r6c8, r6c9≠X → r5c9=X
              box 7 {r7c3, [r8c2=r9c8], r9c2}: [r8c2=r9c8]=X → r7c3≠X
              r5c6=X and r5c9=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r6c8) = color(r7c3) = X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c8, r6c9}: r6c8=X → r6c3, r6c9≠X
              col 8 {r6c8, [r8c2=r9c8], r8c8}: r6c8=X → [r8c2=r9c8], r8c8≠X
              box 6 {r5c9, r6c8, r6c9}: r6c8=X → r5c9≠X
              box 7 {r7c3, [r8c2=r9c8], r9c2}: r7c3=X → r9c2≠X
              row 8 {[r8c2=r9c8], r8c6, r8c8}: [r8c2=r9c8], r8c8≠X → r8c6=X
              row 9 {[r8c2=r9c8], r9c2, r9c6}: [r8c2=r9c8], r9c2≠X → r9c6=X
              col 6 {r5c6, r8c6, r9c6}: r8c6=X and r9c6=X clash
              Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r8c2) ≠ color(r9c8). Add edge.
        3.  Diamond {r8c6, r8c2, r8c8, r9c8} (spine r8c2—r8c8).
            → color(r8c6) = color(r9c8). Identify.
        4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c6, r5c9, r6c8, [r8c6=r9c8]}:
            Diagonals: {r5c6, r6c8} and {r5c9, [r8c6=r9c8]} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r5c6) = color(r6c8) = X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c8, r6c9}: r6c8=X → r6c3, r6c9≠X
              col 6 {r5c6, [r8c6=r9c8], r9c6}: r5c6=X → [r8c6=r9c8], r9c6≠X
              col 8 {r6c8, [r8c6=r9c8], r8c8}: r6c8=X → r8c8≠X
              box 6 {r5c9, r6c8, r6c9}: r6c8=X → r5c9≠X
              row 8 {r8c2, [r8c6=r9c8], r8c8}: [r8c6=r9c8], r8c8≠X → r8c2=X
              row 9 {[r8c6=r9c8], r9c2, r9c6}: [r8c6=r9c8], r9c6≠X → r9c2=X
              box 7 {r7c3, r8c2, r9c2}: r8c2=X and r9c2=X clash
              Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r5c9) = color([r8c6=r9c8]) = X
              row 8 {r8c2, [r8c6=r9c8], r8c8}: [r8c6=r9c8]=X → r8c2, r8c8≠X
              row 9 {[r8c6=r9c8], r9c2, r9c6}: [r8c6=r9c8]=X → r9c2, r9c6≠X

              col 8 {r6c8, [r8c6=r9c8], r8c8}: [r8c6=r9c8]=X → r6c8≠X

              row 6 {r6c3, r6c8, r6c9}: r6c8, r6c9≠X → r6c3=X
              r6c3=X and r7c3=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 2/2 [no_ladder] (diamond+xwing+branch) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r8c2, r9c8:
      Case A: color(r8c2) = color(r9c8). Identify.
        2.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r6c3, r6c8, [r8c2=r9c8], r7c3}:
            Diagonals: {r6c3, [r8c2=r9c8]} and {r6c8, r7c3} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r6c3) = color([r8c2=r9c8]) = X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c8, r6c9}: r6c3=X → r6c8, r6c9≠X
              row 8 {[r8c2=r9c8], r8c6, r8c8}: [r8c2=r9c8]=X → r8c6, r8c8≠X
              row 9 {[r8c2=r9c8], r9c1, r9c6}: [r8c2=r9c8]=X → r9c1, r9c6≠X
              col 6 {r5c6, r8c6, r9c6}: r8c6, r9c6≠X → r5c6=X
              box 6 {r5c9, r6c8, r6c9}: r6c8, r6c9≠X → r5c9=X
              box 7 {r7c3, [r8c2=r9c8], r9c1}: [r8c2=r9c8]=X → r7c3≠X
              r5c6=X and r5c9=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r6c8) = color(r7c3) = X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c8, r6c9}: r6c8=X → r6c3, r6c9≠X
              col 8 {r6c8, [r8c2=r9c8], r8c8}: r6c8=X → [r8c2=r9c8], r8c8≠X
              box 6 {r5c9, r6c8, r6c9}: r6c8=X → r5c9≠X
              box 7 {r7c3, [r8c2=r9c8], r9c1}: r7c3=X → r9c1≠X
              row 8 {[r8c2=r9c8], r8c6, r8c8}: [r8c2=r9c8], r8c8≠X → r8c6=X
              row 9 {[r8c2=r9c8], r9c1, r9c6}: [r8c2=r9c8], r9c1≠X → r9c6=X
              col 6 {r5c6, r8c6, r9c6}: r8c6=X and r9c6=X clash
              Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r8c2) ≠ color(r9c8). Add edge.
        3.  Diamond {r8c6, r8c2, r8c8, r9c8} (spine r8c2—r8c8).
            → color(r8c6) = color(r9c8). Identify.
        4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c6, r5c9, r6c8, [r8c6=r9c8]}:
            Diagonals: {r5c6, r6c8} and {r5c9, [r8c6=r9c8]} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r5c6) = color(r6c8) = X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c8, r6c9}: r6c8=X → r6c3, r6c9≠X
              col 6 {r5c6, [r8c6=r9c8], r9c6}: r5c6=X → [r8c6=r9c8], r9c6≠X
              col 8 {r6c8, [r8c6=r9c8], r8c8}: r6c8=X → r8c8≠X
              box 6 {r5c9, r6c8, r6c9}: r6c8=X → r5c9≠X
              row 8 {r8c2, [r8c6=r9c8], r8c8}: [r8c6=r9c8], r8c8≠X → r8c2=X
              row 9 {[r8c6=r9c8], r9c1, r9c6}: [r8c6=r9c8], r9c6≠X → r9c1=X
              box 7 {r7c3, r8c2, r9c1}: r8c2=X and r9c1=X clash
              Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r5c9) = color([r8c6=r9c8]) = X
              row 8 {r8c2, [r8c6=r9c8], r8c8}: [r8c6=r9c8]=X → r8c2, r8c8≠X
              row 9 {[r8c6=r9c8], r9c1, r9c6}: [r8c6=r9c8]=X → r9c1, r9c6≠X
              col 6 {r5c6, [r8c6=r9c8], r9c6}: [r8c6=r9c8]=X → r5c6≠X
              col 8 {r6c8, [r8c6=r9c8], r8c8}: [r8c6=r9c8]=X → r6c8≠X
              box 6 {r5c9, r6c8, r6c9}: r5c9=X → r6c9≠X

              r6c3=X and r7c3=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.

      → color(r5c6) = color(r6c9). Identify.
  5.  Diamond {[r5c9=r8c6], [r5c6=r6c9], [r6c6=r9c9], [r6c3=r9c2]} (spine [r5c6=r6c9]—[r6c6=r9c9]).
      → color([r5c9=r8c6]) = color([r6c3=r9c2]). Identify.
  6.  K₄ on {[r5c9=r6c3=r8c6=r9c2], [r6c6=r9c9], r8c8, r9c7}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 1/2 [no_diamond] (xwing+oddwheel+branch+guardian) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r7c9, r9c6:
      Case A: color(r7c9) = color(r9c6). Identify.
        2.  Guardian: r6c6 guards oddagon {r6c6, r6c3, r8c3, r9c2, [r7c9=r9c6]} (source r7c3).
            → color(r6c6) = color(r7c3). Identify.
        3.  Odd wheel: hub [r6c6=r7c3] forces rim to 2 colors.
            Bivalue oddagon {r6c3, r6c9, [r7c9=r9c6], r9c2, r8c3} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r7c9) ≠ color(r9c6). Add edge.
        4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c6, r5c9, r7c9, r9c6}:
            Diagonals: {r5c6, r7c9} and {r5c9, r9c6} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r5c6) = color(r7c9) = X
              col 6 {r5c6, r6c6, r9c6}: r5c6=X → r6c6, r9c6≠X
              col 9 {r5c9, r6c9, r7c9}: r7c9=X → r5c9, r6c9≠X
              box 9 {r7c9, r8c7, r8c8}: r7c9=X → r8c7, r8c8≠X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c9}: r6c6, r6c9≠X → r6c3=X
              row 8 {r8c3, r8c7, r8c8}: r8c7, r8c8≠X → r8c3=X
              col 3 {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3}: r6c3=X and r8c3=X clash
              Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r5c9) = color(r9c6) = X
              col 6 {r5c6, r6c6, r9c6}: r9c6=X → r5c6, r6c6≠X
              col 9 {r5c9, r6c9, r7c9}: r5c9=X → r6c9, r7c9≠X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c9}: r6c6, r6c9≠X → r6c3=X
              col 3 {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3}: r6c3=X → r7c3, r8c3≠X
              box 7 {r7c3, r8c3, r9c2}: r7c3, r8c3≠X → r9c2=X
              r9c2=X and r9c6=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

              col 6 {r5c6, r6c6, r7c6}: r5c6=X → r6c6, r7c6≠X

              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c7}: r6c6, r6c7≠X → r6c3=X
              r5c6=X and r6c3=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r7c6) = color(r9c7) = X
              row 9 {r9c1, r9c2, r9c7}: r9c7=X → r9c1, r9c2≠X
              col 6 {r5c6, r6c6, r7c6}: r7c6=X → r5c6, r6c6≠X
              col 7 {r6c7, r7c7, r9c7}: r9c7=X → r6c7, r7c7≠X

              r6c3=X and r8c3=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 3/3 [greedy] (diamond) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r5c6, r5c8, r5c9, r6c7} (spine r5c8—r5c9).

      → color([r6c3=r7c6]) = color(r9c7). Identify.
  5.  K₄ on {[r6c3=r7c6=r9c7], r8c3, r9c1, r9c2}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 3/3 [no_ladder] (set+xwing+branch) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  SET: {row 5, row 6, row 8} − {col 3, col 6, col 9}.
      Remainder: {r8c5, r8c8} = {r7c9, r9c3}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  2.  Branch on r7c9, r8c6:
      Case A: color(r7c9) = color(r8c6). Identify.
        3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c3, r5c9, r6c9, r6c3}:
            Diagonals: {r5c3, r6c9} and {r5c9, r6c3} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r5c3) = color(r6c9) = X
              row 5 {r5c3, r5c6, r5c9}: r5c3=X → r5c6, r5c9≠X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c9}: r6c9=X → r6c3, r6c6≠X
              col 3 {r5c3, r6c3, r9c3}: r5c3=X → r9c3≠X
              col 6 {r5c6, r6c6, [r7c9=r8c6]}: r5c6, r6c6≠X → [r7c9=r8c6]=X
              col 9 {r5c9, r6c9, [r7c9=r8c6]}: r6c9=X and [r7c9=r8c6]=X clash
              Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r5c9) = color(r6c3) = X
              row 5 {r5c3, r5c6, r5c9}: r5c9=X → r5c3, r5c6≠X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c9}: r6c3=X → r6c6, r6c9≠X
              col 3 {r5c3, r6c3, r9c3}: r6c3=X → r9c3≠X
              col 6 {r5c6, r6c6, [r7c9=r8c6]}: r5c6, r6c6≠X → [r7c9=r8c6]=X
              col 9 {r5c9, r6c9, [r7c9=r8c6]}: r5c9=X and [r7c9=r8c6]=X clash
              Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r7c9) ≠ color(r8c6). Add edge.
        4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r7c9, r8c6, r9c4, r9c3}:
            Diagonals: {r7c9, r9c4} and {r8c6, r9c3} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r7c9) = color(r9c4) = X
              col 9 {r5c9, r6c9, r7c9}: r7c9=X → r5c9, r6c9≠X
              box 8 {r8c5, r8c6, r9c4}: r9c4=X → r8c5, r8c6≠X
              row 8 {r8c5, r8c6, r8c8}: r8c5, r8c6≠X → r8c8=X
              r7c9=X and r8c8=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r8c6) = color(r9c3) = X
              row 8 {r8c5, r8c6, r8c8}: r8c6=X → r8c5, r8c8≠X
              col 3 {r5c3, r6c3, r9c3}: r9c3=X → r5c3, r6c3≠X
              col 6 {r5c6, r6c6, r8c6}: r8c6=X → r5c6, r6c6≠X
              box 8 {r8c5, r8c6, r9c4}: r8c6=X → r9c4≠X
              row 5 {r5c3, r5c6, r5c9}: r5c3, r5c6≠X → r5c9=X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c9}: r6c3, r6c6≠X → r6c9=X
              col 9 {r5c9, r6c9, r7c9}: r5c9=X and r6c9=X clash
              Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  2.  Diamond {[r6c8=r9c9], r8c7, r8c8, r8c5} (spine r8c7—r8c8).
      → color([r6c8=r9c9]) = color(r8c5). Identify.
  3.  Odd wheel: hub [r6c8=r8c5=r9c9] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {r6c3, r6c6, r7c6, r9c5, r9c3} (length 5) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 2/3 [no_diamond] (set+branch) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  SET: {row 8, row 9} − {box 8, box 9}.
      Remainder: {r9c3} = {r7c6}.
      → color(r9c3) = color(r7c6). Identify.
  2.  Branch on r6c8, r9c9:
      Case A: color(r6c8) = color(r9c9). Identify.
        3.  K₄ on {r6c3, r6c6, [r6c8=r9c9], [r7c6=r9c3]}. Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r6c8) ≠ color(r9c9). Add edge.
        4.  K₄ on {r4c9, r5c9, r6c8, r9c9}. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r6c8, r4c9, r5c9, r7c9} (spine r4c9—r5c9).
      → color(r6c8) = color(r7c9). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c3, r6c6, [r6c8=r7c9], r7c6} (spine r6c6—[r6c8=r7c9]).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r7c6). Identify.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {[r6c3=r7c6], [r6c8=r7c9], r8c8, r8c5}:
      Diagonals: {[r6c3=r7c6], r8c8} and {[r6c8=r7c9], r8c5} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color([r6c3=r7c6]) = color(r8c8) = X
        row 6 {[r6c3=r7c6], r6c6, [r6c8=r7c9]}: [r6c3=r7c6]=X → r6c6, [r6c8=r7c9]≠X

        box 8 {[r6c3=r7c6], r8c5, r9c6}: r8c5=X and r9c6=X clash
        Contradiction.

=== Alt proof 1/3 [no_diamond] (ladder+hexagon+branch) ===

  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r6c5, r7c6:
      Case A: color(r6c5) = color(r7c6). Identify.
        2.  Circular ladder {r6c3—[r6c5=r7c6], r8c3—r8c6, r9c3—r9c4}:
            Satellites r6c8 (rung 1), r8c9 (rung 2) forced to distinct colors. Add edge.
        3.  K₄ on {r4c9, r5c9, r6c8, r8c9}. Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r6c5) ≠ color(r7c6). Add edge.
        4.  Bridged hexagon: ring {r4c9, r6c8, r6c5, r7c6, r8c6, r8c9}
            Bridges: r5c9—r5c6 (edges r4c9—r6c8 ↔ r7c6—r8c6), r6c3—r8c3 (edges r6c8—r6c5 ↔ r8c6—r8c9), r5c6—r5c9 (edges r6c5—r7c6 ↔ r8c9—r4c9).
            Each bridge forces opposite edges to miss different colors,
            but every 3-coloring of C₆ requires at least one matching pair. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 2/3 [no_oddwheel] (diamond+guardian) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r6c8, r4c9, r5c9, r8c9} (spine r4c9—r5c9).
      → color(r6c8) = color(r8c9). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c5, r6c3, [r6c8=r8c9], r8c3} (spine r6c3—[r6c8=r8c9]).
      → color(r6c5) = color(r8c3). Identify.
  3.  Guardian: r9c4 guards oddagon {r9c4, r8c6, [r6c8=r8c9], r6c3, r9c3} (source [r6c5=r8c3]).
      → color(r9c4) = color([r6c5=r8c3]). Identify.
  4.  K₄ on {r5c6, [r6c5=r8c3=r9c4], r7c6, r8c6}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  5.  K₄ on {[r6c5=r7c6=r8c3], [r6c8=r8c9=r9c3], r8c6, r9c4}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 1/3 [no_oddwheel] (diamond+xwing) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r7c6, r9c4, r9c5, r9c3} (spine r9c4—r9c5).
      → color(r7c6) = color(r9c3). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c6, r6c3, [r7c6=r9c3], r8c3} (spine r6c3—[r7c6=r9c3]).
      → color(r6c6) = color(r8c3). Identify.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r5c6, r5c8, r6c9, [r6c6=r8c3]}:
      Diagonals: {r5c6, r6c9} and {r5c8, [r6c6=r8c3]} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r5c6) = color(r6c9) = X
        row 6 {r6c3, [r6c6=r8c3], r6c9}: r6c9=X → r6c3, [r6c6=r8c3]≠X
        col 3 {r6c3, [r6c6=r8c3], [r7c6=r9c3]}: r6c3, [r6c6=r8c3]≠X → [r7c6=r9c3]=X
        col 6 {r5c6, [r6c6=r8c3], [r7c6=r9c3]}: r5c6=X and [r7c6=r9c3]=X clash
        Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r5c8) = color([r6c6=r8c3]) = X
        row 6 {r6c3, [r6c6=r8c3], r6c9}: [r6c6=r8c3]=X → r6c3, r6c9≠X
        col 3 {r6c3, [r6c6=r8c3], [r7c6=r9c3]}: [r6c6=r8c3]=X → [r7c6=r9c3]≠X
        col 6 {r5c6, [r6c6=r8c3], [r7c6=r9c3]}: [r6c6=r8c3]=X → r5c6≠X
        box 6 {r4c9, r5c8, r6c9}: r5c8=X → r4c9≠X
        col 9 {r4c9, r6c9, r8c9}: r4c9, r6c9≠X → r8c9=X
        [r6c6=r8c3]=X and r8c9=X are adjacent
        Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 1/3 [no_oddwheel] (diamond+set+xwing) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r8c8, r9c8, r9c9, r9c2} (spine r9c8—r9c9).
      → color(r8c8) = color(r9c2). Identify.
  2.  SET: {row 6, row 8, row 9} − {col 3, col 6, col 9}.
      Remainder: {[r8c8=r9c2], r9c8} = {r3c6, r3c9, r7c3}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r3c9, r7c3, [r8c8=r9c2], r9c9}:
      Diagonals: {r3c9, [r8c8=r9c2]} and {r7c3, r9c9} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r3c9) = color([r8c8=r9c2]) = X
        row 8 {r8c3, r8c6, [r8c8=r9c2]}: [r8c8=r9c2]=X → r8c3, r8c6≠X
        row 9 {[r8c8=r9c2], r9c8, r9c9}: [r8c8=r9c2]=X → r9c8, r9c9≠X
        col 9 {r3c9, r6c9, r9c9}: r3c9=X → r6c9≠X
        box 7 {r7c3, r8c3, [r8c8=r9c2]}: [r8c8=r9c2]=X → r7c3≠X
        col 3 {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3}: r7c3, r8c3≠X → r6c3=X
        row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c9}: r6c3=X → r6c6≠X
        col 6 {r3c6, r6c6, r8c6}: r6c6, r8c6≠X → r3c6=X
        r3c6=X and r3c9=X are adjacent
        Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r7c3) = color(r9c9) = X
        row 9 {[r8c8=r9c2], r9c8, r9c9}: r9c9=X → [r8c8=r9c2], r9c8≠X
        col 3 {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3}: r7c3=X → r6c3, r8c3≠X
        col 9 {r3c9, r6c9, r9c9}: r9c9=X → r3c9, r6c9≠X
        row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c9}: r6c3, r6c9≠X → r6c6=X
        row 8 {r8c3, r8c6, [r8c8=r9c2]}: r8c3, [r8c8=r9c2]≠X → r8c6=X
        col 6 {r3c6, r6c6, r8c6}: r6c6=X and r8c6=X clash
        Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

  5.  Diamond {[r3c6=r6c3=r9c2], [r3c9=r6c6], [r6c9=r9c6], r7c9} (spine [r3c9=r6c6]—[r6c9=r9c6]).
      → color([r3c6=r6c3=r9c2]) = color(r7c9). Identify.
  6.  K₄ on {[r3c6=r6c3=r7c9=r9c2], r8c3, r8c7, r8c8}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r3c9, r8c9, r9c9, r8c8} (spine r8c9—r9c9).

      Bridges: r6c8—[r3c9=r8c8] (edges r6c3—r6c6 ↔ r9c9—r8c9), r3c6—[r3c9=r8c8] (edges r6c6—r9c6 ↔ r8c9—r8c3), r9c2—r7c3 (edges r9c6—r9c9 ↔ r8c3—r6c3).

=== Alt proof 1/3 [no_diamond] (xwing+branch+guardian) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Branch on r6c8, r8c3:
      Case A: color(r6c8) = color(r8c3). Identify.
        2.  Guardian: r9c6 guards oddagon {r9c6, r6c6, r6c3, r7c3, r9c2} (source [r6c8=r8c3]).
            → color(r9c6) = color([r6c8=r8c3]). Identify.
        3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r3c6, r3c9, r9c9, [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6]}:
            Diagonals: {r3c6, r9c9} and {r3c9, [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6]} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r3c6) = color(r9c9) = X
              row 9 {[r6c8=r8c3=r9c6], r9c2, r9c9}: r9c9=X → [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6], r9c2≠X
              col 6 {r3c6, r6c6, [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6]}: r3c6=X → r6c6≠X
              col 9 {r3c9, r7c9, r9c9}: r9c9=X → r3c9, r7c9≠X
              box 7 {[r6c8=r8c3=r9c6], r7c3, r9c2}: [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6], r9c2≠X → r7c3=X
              box 9 {r7c9, r8c8, r9c9}: r9c9=X → r8c8≠X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6]}: r6c6, [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6]≠X → r6c3=X
              col 3 {r6c3, [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6], r7c3}: r6c3=X and r7c3=X clash
              Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r3c9) = color([r6c8=r8c3=r9c6]) = X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6]}: [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6]=X → r6c3, r6c6≠X
              row 9 {[r6c8=r8c3=r9c6], r9c2, r9c9}: [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6]=X → r9c2, r9c9≠X
              col 3 {r6c3, [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6], r7c3}: [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6]=X → r7c3≠X
              col 6 {r3c6, r6c6, [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6]}: [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6]=X → r3c6≠X
              col 9 {r3c9, r7c9, r9c9}: r3c9=X → r7c9≠X
              box 9 {r7c9, r8c8, r9c9}: r7c9, r9c9≠X → r8c8=X
              [r6c8=r8c3=r9c6]=X and r8c8=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r6c8) ≠ color(r8c3). Add edge.
        4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r7c3, r7c9, r8c8, r8c3}:
            Diagonals: {r7c3, r8c8} and {r7c9, r8c3} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r7c3) = color(r8c8) = X
              col 3 {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3}: r7c3=X → r6c3, r8c3≠X
              box 7 {r7c3, r8c3, r9c2}: r7c3=X → r9c2≠X
              box 9 {r7c9, r8c8, r9c9}: r8c8=X → r7c9, r9c9≠X
              row 9 {r9c2, r9c6, r9c9}: r9c2, r9c9≠X → r9c6=X
              col 6 {r3c6, r6c6, r9c6}: r9c6=X → r3c6, r6c6≠X
              col 9 {r3c9, r7c9, r9c9}: r7c9, r9c9≠X → r3c9=X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c8}: r6c3, r6c6≠X → r6c8=X
              r6c8=X and r8c8=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r7c9) = color(r8c3) = X
              col 3 {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3}: r8c3=X → r6c3, r7c3≠X
              col 9 {r3c9, r7c9, r9c9}: r7c9=X → r3c9, r9c9≠X
              box 7 {r7c3, r8c3, r9c2}: r8c3=X → r9c2≠X
              box 9 {r7c9, r8c8, r9c9}: r7c9=X → r8c8≠X
              row 9 {r9c2, r9c6, r9c9}: r9c2, r9c9≠X → r9c6=X
              col 6 {r3c6, r6c6, r9c6}: r9c6=X → r3c6, r6c6≠X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c8}: r6c3, r6c6≠X → r6c8=X
              r6c8=X and r8c3=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      → color(r3c9) = color(r5c8). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3, r9c2} (spine r7c3—r8c3).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r9c2). Identify.
  3.  Diamond {r6c9, [r6c3=r9c2], r6c6, r9c6} (spine [r6c3=r9c2]—r6c6).
      → color(r6c9) = color(r9c6). Identify.
  4.  Diamond {[r3c9=r5c8], r3c6, [r6c9=r9c6], r6c6} (spine r3c6—[r6c9=r9c6]).
      → color([r3c9=r5c8]) = color(r6c6). Identify.
  5.  K₄ on {[r3c9=r5c8=r6c6], [r6c3=r9c2], [r6c9=r9c6], r9c8}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

        5.  K₄ on {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3, r9c2}. Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 2/3 [no_diamond] (set+xwing+branch) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  SET: {row 5, row 9} − {box 6, box 7}.
      Remainder: {r5c6, r9c9} = {r6c9, r8c3}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  2.  Branch on r5c6, r6c3:
      Case A: color(r5c6) = color(r6c3). Identify.
        3.  K₄ on {[r5c6=r6c3], r5c7, r5c8, r6c9}. Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r5c6) ≠ color(r6c3). Add edge.
        4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r3c6, r3c9, r9c9, r5c6}:
            Diagonals: {r3c6, r9c9} and {r3c9, r5c6} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r3c6) = color(r9c9) = X
              row 9 {r9c1, r9c2, r9c9}: r9c9=X → r9c1, r9c2≠X
              col 6 {r3c6, r5c6, r6c6}: r3c6=X → r5c6, r6c6≠X
              col 9 {r3c9, r6c9, r9c9}: r9c9=X → r3c9, r6c9≠X
              box 7 {r8c3, r9c1, r9c2}: r9c1, r9c2≠X → r8c3=X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c9}: r6c6, r6c9≠X → r6c3=X
              r6c3=X and r8c3=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r3c9) = color(r5c6) = X
              row 5 {r5c6, r5c7, r5c8}: r5c6=X → r5c7, r5c8≠X
              col 6 {r3c6, r5c6, r6c6}: r5c6=X → r3c6, r6c6≠X
              col 9 {r3c9, r6c9, r9c9}: r3c9=X → r6c9, r9c9≠X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c9}: r6c6, r6c9≠X → r6c3=X
              r5c6=X and r6c3=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

        col 3 {[r5c3=r6c9], r8c3, [r8c9=r9c3]}: [r8c9=r9c3]=X → [r5c3=r6c9]≠X
        col 6 {r3c6, r7c6, r8c6}: r3c6=X → r7c6≠X
        col 9 {r3c9, [r5c3=r6c9], [r8c9=r9c3]}: [r8c9=r9c3]=X → r3c9≠X
        box 8 {r7c6, r8c6, r9c5}: r7c6, r8c6≠X → r9c5=X
        [r8c9=r9c3]=X and r9c5=X are adjacent
        Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r3c9) = color(r8c6) = X
        row 8 {r8c3, r8c6, [r8c9=r9c3]}: r8c6=X → r8c3, [r8c9=r9c3]≠X
        col 3 {[r5c3=r6c9], r8c3, [r8c9=r9c3]}: r8c3, [r8c9=r9c3]≠X → [r5c3=r6c9]=X
        col 6 {r3c6, r7c6, r8c6}: r8c6=X → r3c6, r7c6≠X
        col 9 {r3c9, [r5c3=r6c9], [r8c9=r9c3]}: r3c9=X and [r5c3=r6c9]=X clash
        Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 1/3 [no_xwing] (diamond+oddwheel) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r5c3, r6c1, r6c2, r6c9} (spine r6c1—r6c2).
      → color(r5c3) = color(r6c9). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {[r5c3=r6c9], r8c3, r8c9, r8c6} (spine r8c3—r8c9).
      → color([r5c3=r6c9]) = color(r8c6). Identify.
  3.  Odd wheel: hub [r5c3=r6c9=r8c6] forces rim to 2 colors.
      Bivalue oddagon {r3c6, r3c9, r8c9, r8c3, r9c3, r9c5, r7c6} (length 7) cannot be 2-colored. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  Diamond {r6c3, r7c3, r8c3, r9c2} (spine r7c3—r8c3).
      → color(r6c3) = color(r9c2). Identify.
  2.  Diamond {r6c6, [r6c3=r9c2], r9c6, r9c8} (spine [r6c3=r9c2]—r9c6).
      → color(r6c6) = color(r9c8). Identify.
  3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r3c6, r3c9, r6c9, [r6c6=r9c8]}:
      Diagonals: {r3c6, r6c9} and {r3c9, [r6c6=r9c8]} (non-adjacent).
      By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
      Case 1: color(r3c6) = color(r6c9) = X
        row 6 {[r6c3=r9c2], [r6c6=r9c8], r6c9}: r6c9=X → [r6c3=r9c2], [r6c6=r9c8]≠X

        Contradiction.
      Case 2: color(r3c9) = color([r6c6=r9c8]) = X

        col 6 {r3c6, [r6c6=r9c8], r9c6}: [r6c6=r9c8]=X → r3c6≠X
        col 9 {r3c9, r4c9, r6c9}: r3c9=X → r4c9≠X
        box 6 {r4c9, r5c8, r6c9}: r4c9, r6c9≠X → r5c8=X
        r5c8=X and [r6c6=r9c8]=X are adjacent
        Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

      → color(r8c8) = color(r9c5). Identify.
  2.  SET: {row 3, row 6, row 8} − {col 3, col 6, col 9}.
      Remainder: {r8c5, [r8c8=r9c5]} = {r7c9, r9c3}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  3.  Circular ladder {r3c3—r6c3, r3c6—r6c6, r3c9—r6c9}:
      Satellites r9c3 (rung 1), r8c6 (rung 2), r7c9 (rung 3) forced to distinct colors. Add triangle.
  4.  K₄ on {r7c9, r8c6, [r8c8=r9c5], r9c3}. Contradiction.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □

=== Alt proof 3/3 [no_ladder] (set+xwing+branch) ===
Proof of non-3-colorability:
  Assume for contradiction it is 3-colorable.

  1.  SET: {row 3, row 6, row 8} − {col 3, col 6, col 9}.
      Remainder: {r8c5, r8c8} = {r7c9, r9c3}.
      → Both sides forced all-distinct. Virtual edges added.
  2.  Branch on r7c9, r8c6:
      Case A: color(r7c9) = color(r8c6). Identify.
        3.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r3c3, r3c9, r6c9, r6c3}:
            Diagonals: {r3c3, r6c9} and {r3c9, r6c3} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r3c3) = color(r6c9) = X
              row 3 {r3c3, r3c6, r3c9}: r3c3=X → r3c6, r3c9≠X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c9}: r6c9=X → r6c3, r6c6≠X
              col 3 {r3c3, r6c3, r9c3}: r3c3=X → r9c3≠X
              col 6 {r3c6, r6c6, [r7c9=r8c6]}: r3c6, r6c6≠X → [r7c9=r8c6]=X
              col 9 {r3c9, r6c9, [r7c9=r8c6]}: r6c9=X and [r7c9=r8c6]=X clash
              Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r3c9) = color(r6c3) = X
              row 3 {r3c3, r3c6, r3c9}: r3c9=X → r3c3, r3c6≠X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c9}: r6c3=X → r6c6, r6c9≠X
              col 3 {r3c3, r6c3, r9c3}: r6c3=X → r9c3≠X
              col 6 {r3c6, r6c6, [r7c9=r8c6]}: r3c6, r6c6≠X → [r7c9=r8c6]=X
              col 9 {r3c9, r6c9, [r7c9=r8c6]}: r3c9=X and [r7c9=r8c6]=X clash
              Contradiction.
      Case B: color(r7c9) ≠ color(r8c6). Add edge.
        4.  Pigeonhole X-wing on {r7c9, r8c6, r9c5, r9c3}:
            Diagonals: {r7c9, r9c5} and {r8c6, r9c3} (non-adjacent).
            By pigeonhole, one diagonal must share a color.
            Case 1: color(r7c9) = color(r9c5) = X
              col 9 {r3c9, r6c9, r7c9}: r7c9=X → r3c9, r6c9≠X
              box 8 {r8c5, r8c6, r9c5}: r9c5=X → r8c5, r8c6≠X
              row 8 {r8c5, r8c6, r8c8}: r8c5, r8c6≠X → r8c8=X
              r7c9=X and r8c8=X are adjacent
              Contradiction.
            Case 2: color(r8c6) = color(r9c3) = X
              row 8 {r8c5, r8c6, r8c8}: r8c6=X → r8c5, r8c8≠X
              col 3 {r3c3, r6c3, r9c3}: r9c3=X → r3c3, r6c3≠X
              col 6 {r3c6, r6c6, r8c6}: r8c6=X → r3c6, r6c6≠X
              box 8 {r8c5, r8c6, r9c5}: r8c6=X → r9c5≠X
              row 3 {r3c3, r3c6, r3c9}: r3c3, r3c6≠X → r3c9=X
              row 6 {r6c3, r6c6, r6c9}: r6c3, r6c6≠X → r6c9=X
              col 9 {r3c9, r6c9, r7c9}: r3c9=X and r6c9=X clash
              Contradiction.
      Both cases contradict 3-colorability.

  Therefore the pattern is not 3-colorable. □
